Disneyland's Response To Mysterious "UFO" Video Captured Above The Resort Buzzes Fans Even More
Source: TheTravel    Published: 2025-11-16 16:26:00

Stacey Sloughfy is a freelance travel writer and blogger with a deep love for exploring the world. In addition to TheTravel, her work has been featured in GoAbroad and WeSaidGoTravel. While her favorite destinations include Japan, Costa Rica, Mexico, and Maui, she's always ready for a road trip across the U.S. With a B.S. in Agriculture from the University of Kentucky, Stacey spent 26 years in scientific labs before returning to school to earn a certificate in technical writing. When she's not writing or traveling, you'll find her tending to her garden or curled up with her two cats at home in southern Indiana, planning her next adventure. A strange, perfectly circular ring floating above Disneyland Resort stopped early morning drivers in their tracks on Thursday, quickly igniting online chatter about UFOs, illusions, and everything in between. The timing only heightened the buzz—Disney World Florida has had guests on edge over the last month due to a string of deaths, and now UFO sightings at Disneyland California have fans wondering what on earth is happening across the parks. Cell phone videos of the dark ring rising over Anaheim spread fast, with viewers unable to decide whether the moment was eerie, mesmerizing, or just plain baffling. But the mystery didn't last long. As speculation swirled, Disneyland stepped in with a simple explanation that longtime fans recognized instantly—one that only fueled even more discussion about the park's behind-the-scenes magic. So what was the mysterious ring drifting above the Happiest Place on Earth, and why does it keep catching people off guard? Disneyland moved quickly to clear up the confusion once the early morning footage began circulating. The resort confirmed that the strange ring wasn't anything extraterrestrial but rather a byproduct of a pyrotechnic test conducted before the park opened for the day. For longtime visitors, this explanation rang familiar. Shows like World of Color and Fantasmic! are known for their fire effects, which can occasionally send a concentrated plume swirling into a perfect circle when the air is still. One of the first people to capture the spectacle shared photos and video after spotting the ring hovering above the resort around 6:30am. Lori Nayahalski told KTLA, "It wasn't dissipating, nor was it a flock of birds. Real life Matrix or just an orchestrated spoof... I don't know, but it was something." While Disneyland's clarification settled the UFO debate, it also highlighted just how little most casual visitors know about the park's nightly production work. And it turns out this wasn't the first time guests have been startled by the exact same phenomenon. Although these rings look mysterious, they're not part of the show. They're an unintended side effect of specific fire bursts used in Disneyland's nighttime spectaculars. Longtime Disneyland fans quickly began comparing this week's footage with other sightings from recent years. In a Reddit post from several months ago, one visitor described an almost identical moment: "We saw this in the sky over Disneyland about 9:15pm. There was no noise... It was pretty high in the sky and quite large in diameter." Their family only noticed it because their child pointed it out. Other commenters chimed in to explain that the rings appear after certain fire sequences, especially during World of Color. "Happens after World of Color :) Have seen it several times. It's from the fire portion of the show." Another guest added that the same thing occurs with pyrotechnic blasts in Fantasmic!: "Yeah, the giant fire blast in the middle of World of Color does this. ... I believe a few of the fire effects in Fantasmic cause them too." For theme park diehards, the phenomenon feels almost routine. But for guests who don't catch Disneyland's major nighttime productions, or who witness the rings unexpectedly, without the surrounding music and lights, the sight can be genuinely startling. Combine that with the right lighting conditions and a quiet morning sky, and the result is a mystery that feels much bigger than it really is. Although the strange ring that hovered above the resort wasn't a UFO, the moment highlighted how the park's pyrotechnic artistry, usually seen only as a part of a carefully choreographed show, can occasionally create real-world surprises that feel otherworldly. For many fans, the incident is just another reminder that Disneyland's magic extends far beyond the ground. We want to hear from you! Source: Daily Star    Published: 2025-11-16 15:19:00

Russia's invasion of Ukraine could soon be brought to an end, according to one pro-Putin psychic. It comes as the Kremlin continues to strike targets deep inside Ukraine as the brutal war continues. Dictator Vladimir Putin is showing no sign of stopping his brutal invasion of Ukraine, as it hurtles toward the four-year anniversary of the full-scale war getting underway. Meanwhile, Kyiv and Moscow are drifting further away from reaching a peace deal as Russia remains a pariah on the world stage. But for one mystic, who is loyal to Russia's president, she sees a close end in sight to the war, with victory for Russia an inevitability. She added that the war will end "with a surprise" for Western leaders, as she gives a chilling warning. Pro-Kremlin outlet MK reported that psychic Adelina Panina is convinced that Ukraine will surrender to Putin incredibly soon. This comes despite the fact that Russia has been crippled by Western sanctions as it continues to offer full support to Ukraine. Adelina said: "The situation with the end of the Second Military District is already in the final stretch." She referred to the seized Ukrainian land that Russia currently occupies, before adding: "The whole world understands that our troops have complete control of the front and will not relinquish it. "No new arms deliveries will change the situation; as I've said repeatedly, our ill-wishers are doing everything they can to prolong the fighting. "So far, they've succeeded, but there's a high probability that the situation with the Second Military District will be completely concluded by 2026." She added that the end of the war will be an "abrupt and unexpected" end, as she insists that Europe will not be happy with the results at the end of the war. Supposedly 'predicting the future', she said: "There will be some final agreement that will surprise the European countries, especially those that have been opposing our country all this time and trying to put a spoke in its wheel. "Of course, European politicians will be very unhappy," Adelina predicted. "There will be outrage, but they will have no choice." Panina went on to say that Russia's win in the war is guaranteed in the stars, with her predicting that all of the wartime goals stated by Mad Vlad will be achieved. However, she did warn that Russia itself will not enjoy the fruits of its labour in invading Ukraine, but Russia's "opponents" will instead. Adelina's comments come after Ukraine was bombarded with its latest set of strikes from Moscow in scenes that were described as "astonishingly lethal", according to the BBC. Ukraine, for its part, is striking back where it can, targeting an oil refinery in the region of Ryazan on Saturday (November 15). The Kremlin, usually unwilling to admit such heavy losses, confirmed the factory had been targeted and revealed it was heavily damaged. It comes as a major blow to Putin's war machine. However, the governor of the region, Pavel Malkov, did not explicitly say that Ukraine was directly responsible; instead, he claimed 25 Ukrainian drones were shot down - but the debris caused the damage. Fractured fingers! Urine! Magic! 'Now You See Me: Now You Don't' cast dishes movie details
Source: USA Today    Published: 2025-11-16 14:07:42

NEW YORK — Rosamund Pike raves about the sights and the scenes while filming "Now You See Me: Now You Don't" in Budapest and Abu Dhabi. However, the actress points out one major on-set difference from past projects. "The cast members were practicing their card tricks," Pike, 46, recalls to USA TODAY. "Everyone's saying, 'Do you wanna see a trick?'" There's plenty of sleight of hand in the third installment of the "Now You See Me" magician-driven, thriller franchise (in theaters now). The original Four Horsemen (Jesse Eisenberg, Isla Fisher, Woody Harrelson, Dave Franco) team up with a new group of Horsemen (Justice Smith, Dominic Sessa, Ariana Greenblatt) to stop a villain (Pike) from selling the world's largest diamond to an evil entity. "I like bringing my big villain energy to the screen," Pike says with a laugh, calling it her "BVE." "It's more fun to see someone who's vain and full of themselves and who has put themselves on a bit of a pedestal fall down from that pedestal than it is to see someone who's just playing it safer," she says. For Eisenberg, things weren't always safe on set. The actor took part in a fight scene in a room that spins upside down. Everything in the room was padded with styrofoam, save the one bookcase where Eisenberg filmed most of his parts. "You can see my finger is still a little bent there," says Eisenberg, 42, holding up his right hand and pointing to his middle finger. Eisenberg thinks he fractured it, and he wore a cast for the rest of production. "It was really a lot of fun up until that exact moment." Fisher didn't suffer any injuries. But the actress points out another scene where she's stuck in a glass box that's rapidly filling with sand, and then water. Fisher says the scene took a week to film. "At the beginning, people asked to leave the tank to go to the bathroom," Fisher, 49, says. "But I felt like later on, people stopped asking, which made me concerned that some people may be urinating in the water." Without dropping any spoilers, Fisher had good reason to be concerned. Of all the Horsemen trapped in the glass box, she spent the most time underwater. Harrelson shows up to the interview with a deck of cards. He's got a trick up his sleeve, asking costar Morgan Freeman what hand he'd want to be dealt in a game of poker. Excluding a royal flush, Freeman chooses three aces. Harrelson, who has been shuffling this deck of cards the entire time, then proceeds to deal the actor exactly what he asked for. The surprises weren't done: As our interview winds down, a familiar voice is heard off camera asking Harrelson to reshuffle the cards while facing the camera so that we could better see the trick. The voice is of famed illusionist David Blaine. "You didn't show that the cards were shuffled," Blaine explains. "So it could seem like (Freeman) said the aces, and it was set up." Blaine went on to break down what he witnessed. "What I saw happen is legitimately I swear to God, (Freeman) said three aces," he continues. "(Harrelson) was not prepared for it. Woody was shuffling the deck and then he pulled three aces, which is an incredible thing. He actually pulled the aces out of the deck and felt them. It's advanced sleight of hand, what he did." Harrelson and Blaine are friends, and the magician joined the cast at a dinner in New York that evening. The next day, those in attendance were buzzing about what happened. "He ate a wine glass," Smith, 30, reveals. "And then we took a photo, and he somehow changed the photo on the phone without touching it." Greenblatt also recalls Blaine changing the writing on a pen from "Sharpie" to the five of hearts, which was the card she picked. All three of the new Horsemen say they appreciate magic in a new way after filming "Now You See Me 3." But that doesn't change how blown away they were by what Blaine did at dinner. "What (Blaine) does is real magic," Smith says. "That's like actual supernatural magic. Like, he's a wizard."

West Virginia Combining Rich History and Haunted Lore to Offer One of the Most Unique Paranormal Tourism Experiences in US
Source: Travel And Tour World    Published: 2025-11-16 01:14:50

Published on November 16, 2025 West Virginia, a state celebrated for its natural beauty and deep-rooted history, has recently emerged as a prime destination for paranormal tourism. With ghost tours, haunted history walks, and supernatural-themed experiences capturing the imagination of travelers, the Mountain State has found an unexpected way to attract visitors. While interest in paranormal activities is growing, it doesn't necessarily reflect a widespread belief in the supernatural. Instead, it's a testament to the allure of West Virginia's rich storytelling tradition, cultural heritage, and the viral power of social media.Paranormal Tours: A Rising Attraction in West VirginiaAs the air cools and fall sets in, West Virginia's ghost tours and supernatural experiences have gained significant popularity. These tours often highlight the state's unique history, from Civil War battlefields to abandoned mining towns. One standout location is the Trans-Allegheny Lunatic Asylum in Weston, a stunning example of hand-cut stone architecture. This historic site has embraced paranormal tourism, using ghost tours to both raise awareness and fund critical restoration efforts.Advertisement These nighttime tours offer an intriguing blend of education and entertainment, allowing visitors to explore West Virginia's past through a lens of mystery and the supernatural. Visitors are drawn in by tales of tragic events and eerie encounters, learning about the state's history while experiencing the thrill of the unknown. Whether it's a Civil War soldier's ghost or a miner's lingering spirit, the stories add a chilling layer to the state's rich historical tapestry.The Role of Heritage in Paranormal AppealThe success of paranormal tourism in West Virginia can largely be attributed to the state's deep cultural and historical significance. The state's rugged mountains, remote valleys, and forgotten towns are naturally suited to the ghost stories that have been passed down through generations. These tales often weave together real historical events with supernatural elements, creating experiences that resonate with visitors seeking both thrills and a deeper connection to the past.Advertisement Many towns and communities across the state have capitalized on this heritage, offering ghost tours that highlight the state's Civil War history, industrial past, and local folklore. By incorporating real-life tragedies, such as deadly mining accidents or the haunting memories of war, these tours provide visitors with a connection to history that goes beyond mere facts. They allow tourists to experience the state's past in a more personal and memorable way, blending storytelling with the authentic ambiance of old, often derelict, buildings.Social Media's Role in Expanding the Paranormal ExperienceOne of the driving forces behind the rise of paranormal tourism in West Virginia is the impact of social media. Platforms like Instagram, TikTok, and YouTube have amplified interest in the state's ghostly offerings, as tourists share their spine-chilling experiences with a wider audience. The ability to capture and share paranormal encounters has become a major attraction for many, turning these ghost tours into viral phenomena.Advertisement Ghost tours are not only low-cost and low-risk but also offer visitors the chance to create compelling content. Social media users can share eerie photos, videos, and first-hand accounts of their experiences, attracting new audiences eager to visit the same haunted locations. Influencers and content creators have played a key role in spreading the word about West Virginia's paranormal tourism scene, generating buzz and encouraging others to take part in the fun. The social media effect has turned ghost tours into an experience that is both thrilling and shareable, enhancing their appeal to younger travelers and those seeking Instagram-worthy moments.West Virginia: The Ideal Setting for Paranormal ExplorationWest Virginia's landscape provides the perfect atmosphere for paranormal tourism. From the misty hills and secluded towns to the abandoned sites that dot the state, the natural setting amplifies the eerie atmosphere. Whether it's an old mining town with a tragic history or a Civil War battlefield where spirits are said to linger, the state's hauntingly beautiful locations are the ideal backdrop for supernatural exploration.Communities like Harpers Ferry, which played a significant role during the Civil War, offer a glimpse into the past while providing opportunities for ghostly encounters. These areas are steeped in history, making them perfect locations for visitors seeking a mix of history and the supernatural. West Virginia's combination of scenic beauty, historical landmarks, and ghostly tales makes it a prime destination for those looking to embark on a paranormal adventure.What the Future Holds for Paranormal TourismLooking toward the future, paranormal tourism in West Virginia is expected to continue thriving. Industry experts predict that as long as ghost tours remain grounded in authentic local history, they will continue to attract visitors. While the state also promotes its outdoor recreation, heritage, and small-town experiences, paranormal tourism offers a unique way to draw visitors during quieter seasons. It provides an exciting way for travelers to engage with the past, all while adding an element of thrill and mystery.With the continued growth of the official West Virginia Paranormal Trail and more communities embracing the trend, the state is solidifying its reputation as a top destination for paranormal enthusiasts. By blending its rich historical heritage with a modern twist on entertainment, West Virginia has created a tourism experience that appeals to a wide range of interests. Paranormal tourism is not just a seasonal attraction; it's a lasting way to engage visitors with the state's fascinating past and spine-chilling mysteries.Advertisement Share On:Tags: paranormal tourism, Tourism news, US, West VirginiaSubscribe to our NewslettersFollow Travel And Tour World in Google News As the air cools and fall sets in, West Virginia's ghost tours and supernatural experiences have gained significant popularity. These tours often highlight the state's unique history, from Civil War battlefields to abandoned mining towns. One standout location is the Trans-Allegheny Lunatic Asylum in Weston, a stunning example of hand-cut stone architecture. This historic site has embraced paranormal tourism, using ghost tours to both raise awareness and fund critical restoration efforts.Advertisement These nighttime tours offer an intriguing blend of education and entertainment, allowing visitors to explore West Virginia's past through a lens of mystery and the supernatural. Visitors are drawn in by tales of tragic events and eerie encounters, learning about the state's history while experiencing the thrill of the unknown. Whether it's a Civil War soldier's ghost or a miner's lingering spirit, the stories add a chilling layer to the state's rich historical tapestry.The Role of Heritage in Paranormal AppealThe success of paranormal tourism in West Virginia can largely be attributed to the state's deep cultural and historical significance. The state's rugged mountains, remote valleys, and forgotten towns are naturally suited to the ghost stories that have been passed down through generations. These tales often weave together real historical events with supernatural elements, creating experiences that resonate with visitors seeking both thrills and a deeper connection to the past.Advertisement Many towns and communities across the state have capitalized on this heritage, offering ghost tours that highlight the state's Civil War history, industrial past, and local folklore. By incorporating real-life tragedies, such as deadly mining accidents or the haunting memories of war, these tours provide visitors with a connection to history that goes beyond mere facts. They allow tourists to experience the state's past in a more personal and memorable way, blending storytelling with the authentic ambiance of old, often derelict, buildings.Social Media's Role in Expanding the Paranormal ExperienceOne of the driving forces behind the rise of paranormal tourism in West Virginia is the impact of social media. Platforms like Instagram, TikTok, and YouTube have amplified interest in the state's ghostly offerings, as tourists share their spine-chilling experiences with a wider audience.
